A. 6 Color Plotter-Printer Control Codes

A.6.1 Control codes used in the text mode

ｷ Text code ($01)

Sets the printer in the text mode.

ｷ Graphic code ($02)                                    Same as the BASIC MODE GR statement.

Sets the printer in the graphic mode.

ｷ Line up ($03)                                         Same as the BASIC SKIP-1 statement.

Moves the paper one line in the reverse direction. The line counter is decremented by 1.

ｷ Pen test ($04)                                        Same as the BASIC TEST statement.

Writes the following patterns to start ink flowing from the pens, then sets scale = 1 (40 chr/line),

color = 0.

Black       Blue Green              Red

ｷ Reduction scale ($09) + ($09) + ($09)

Reduces the scale from 1 to 0 (80 chr/line).

ｷ Reduction cancel ($09) + ($09) + (SOB)

Enlarges the scale from 0 to 1. (40 chr/line).

ｷ Line counter set ($09) + ($09) + (ASCII)2 + (ASCII)! + (ASCII)0 + (SOD)

                                                        Same as the BASIC PAGE statement.

Specifies the number of lines per page as indicated by 3 bytes of ASCII code. The maximum number of

lines per page is 255. Set to 66 when the power is turned on or the system is reset.

ｷ Line feed ($0A)                                       Same as the BASIC SKIP 1 statement.

Moves the paper one line in the forward direction. The line counter is incremented by 1.

ｷ Magnify scale ($0B)

Enlarges the scale from 1 to 2 (26 chr/line).

ｷ Magnify cancel ($0C)

Reduces the scale from 2 to 1.

ｷ Carriage return ($0D)

Moves the carriage to the left side of the print area.

ｷ Back space ($0E)

Moves the carriage one column to the left. This code is ignored when the carriage is at the left side

of the print area.

ｷ Form feed ($OF)

Moves the paper to the beginning of the next page and resets the line counter to 0.

ｷ Next color ($ ID)

Changes the pen to the next color.

A.6.2 Character scale

ｷ The character scale is automatically set to 1 (40 chr/line) when the power is turned on. Afterwards,
   it can be changed by the control codes and commands.

ｷ In the graphic mode, the scale can be changed in the range from 0 to 63.
ｷ The scale is set to 1 when the mode is switched from graphic to text.
A.6.3 Graphic mode commands

A. 6. 3. 1 Command type

   In the graphic mode, the printer can be controlled by outputting the following commands to the printer.
   Words in parentheses are BASIC statements which have the same functions as the graphic mode com-
mands.

Command name               Format                                                    Function
                                                         Specifies the type of line (solid or dotted) and
LINE TYPE               Lp (p = 0 to 15)                 the dot pitch.
                                                         p = 0 : solid line, p = 1 -- 15 : dotted line p p
ALL INITIALIZE          A
                                                         Sets the printer in the text mode.
HOME (PHOME)            H                                Lifts the pen and returns it to the origin (home
                                                         position).
INITIALIZE (HSET) I
                                                         Sets the current pen location as the origin
DRAW       (LINE)       Dx, y, . . . xn, yn              (x = 0, y = 0).
                        (-999 ^ x , y < 999)
                                                         Draws lines from the current pen location to
RELATIVE DRAW           J A X , Ay . . . Axn, Ayn        coordinates (xj, yj), then to coordinates
               (RLINE)  ( - 9 9 9 < AX, Ay < 9 9 9 )     ( x 2 ' Y2 )> a n d so forth.
                                                         Draws lines from the current pen location to
MOVE (MOVE)             Mx, y                            relative coordinates (axj , Ayj), then to relative
                        (--999 < x, y < 999)             coordinates (AX2 , AY2) and so forth.

             (RMOVE)                                     Lifts the pen and moves it to coordinates (x, y).
                        (-999 < A X , Ay < 999)

           (PCOLOR)     Cn (n = 0 to 3)                  ( A X , Ay).

SCALE SET               Sn (n = 0 to 63)                 Changes the pen color to n.

                                                         Specifies the direction in which characters are
PRINT                   P c ! c 2 c 3 . . . cn (n = ｰｰ)  printed.
                        Xp, q, r (p = 0 or 1)
AXIS       (AXIS)       (q = - 9 9 9 to 999)             Prints characters.
                        (r= 1 to 255)
                                                         Draws an X axis when p = 1 and a Y axis when
                                                         p = 0. q specifies the scale pitch and r specifies
                                                         the number of scale marks to be drawn.

A. 6. 3. 2 Command format

   There are 5 types of command formats as shown below.
1. Command character only (without parameters)

       "A", H , I
2. Command character plus one parameter

       "L", "C", S , Q
3. Command character plus pairs of parameters

         D , J , M, R
         , is used to separate parameters, and a CR code is used to end the parameter list.
4. Command plus character string
         P
       The character string is terminated with a CR code.

,, ., 5. Command plus three parameters
     x
       "," is used to separate parameters.

                                                                                                                                                      199-
     A. 6. 3. 3 Parameter specification
     1. Leading blanks are ignored.
     2. Any number preceded by " -- " is treated as a negative number.
     3. If the number of digits of a number exceeds 3, only the lower 3 digits are effective.
     4. Each parameter is ended with "," or a CR code. If other than numbers are included in a parameter,

            subsequent characters are ignored until a comma or CR code is detected.
            Example) D ^ - 1 3 5 . 2 1 ,

                                   t Ignored.---
     A. 6. 3. 4 Abbreviated formats
     1. Any command can be followed by a one-character command without entering a CR code.

            Ex) " HD100, 200" CR is effective and is the same as "H" CR " D100, 200" CR.
     2. Any command can be followed by a command with one parameter by separating them with a

            comma ",".
            Ex) " LO, S1, Q0, C1, D100, 20011 CR is effective.
     3. A command with pairs of parameters must be terminated with a CR code.
     4. 6. 3. 5 Data change due to mode switching
         The following data changes when the printer is switched from the graphic mode to the text mode.
         ｷ X and Y coordinates
             Y is set to 0 and the origin is placed at the left side of the printable area.
         ｷ Direction of characters
             Q is set to 0.
         ｷ Character scale
            Character scale is set to 1.
         ｷ The line type setting is not affected.

A. 7 Notes Concerning Operation

ｷ Data recorder

ｷ Although the data recorder of the MZ-700 is highly reliable, the read/write head will wear out after
   prolonged use. Further, magnetic particles and dust will accumulate on the head, degrading read/write
   performance. Therefore, the head must be cleaned periodically or replaced when it becomes worn.
    1. To clean the head, open the cassette compartment, press the I PLAY | key, and wipe the head
           and pinch roller using a cotton swab. If they are very dirty, soak the cotton swab in alcohol.
   2. When the head becomes worn, contact your dealer. Do not attempt to replace it by yourself.

ｷ Cassette tape

ｷ Any commercially available cassette tape can                   Slack
   be used with the MZ-700. However, it is re-                 /
   commended that you use quality cassette
   tape produced by a reliable manufacturer.           (oiirn d>
   ｷ Use normal type tapes.                              T T Slack
   ｷ Avoid using C-120 type cassette tapes.
   ｷ Use of C-60 or shorter cassette tapes is        Remove record lock-out
       recommended.                                  tab with a screwdriver.
   ｷ Be sure to take up any the slack in the tape
       with a pencil or the like as shown at right                             Tab for side A
       before loading the cassette tape: otherwise,               Tab for side B
       the tape may break or become wound round
       the pinch roller.

ｷ Protecting programs/data from accidental erasure

   The data recorder of the MZ-700 is equipped
with a write protect function which operates in
the same manner as with ordinary audio cassette
tape decks.

   To prevent data from being accidentally erased,
remove the record lock-out tab from the cassette
with a screwdriver or the like. This makes it
impossible to press the | RECORD key, prevent-
ing erasure of, valuable data.

ｷ Other

   ｷ See page 109 for commercially available cassette tape decks.
ｷ Display unit

   When using a display unit other than one specified for the MZ-700, the screen size must be adjusted.
   See page 106.

                                                                                               201-
ｷ Color plotter-printer

ｷ Do not rotate the pen drum in the reverse direction when replacing pens.
ｷ Be sure to remove the pens from the pen drum, replace their caps to them, and store them in the case

   to prevent them from drying out when the printer is not to be used for an extended period of time.
ｷ It takes a certain amount of time for ink on the paper to dry. (The ink is water-soluble.)
ｷ Do not rip off the paper when the printer cover is removed. Hold down the paper holder when ripping

   off the paper.
ｷ Do not touch the internal mechanism when replacing the pens. Failure to observe this warning may

   result in damage to the printer.
ｷ The color plotter printer generates sound' for a moment when the power is turned on. This is not

   a problem.
ｷ Letters printed in the 80 character line mode may be difficult to read. In this case, use the 40 character/

   line mode.
ｷ In the graphic mode, lines printed repeatedly may become blurred. This is particularly liable to occur

   when a dotted line is printed repeatedly. Due to the characteristics of the ball pen, this is unavoidable.

ｷ Notes concerning software

ｷ It takes about 3 minutes to load the BASIC interpreter.
ｷ The reset switch on the rear panel is to used in the following cases. (See 3. 1. 1.)

   To stop execution of a BASIC program during normal execution or when the program enters an infinite
   loop. To return to the program, use the # command. However, the program or hardware should be
   checked if the program loops.

ｷ BASIC calculation error

ｷ BASIC converts decimal values to floating point binary values before performing calculations, then
   converts the binary calculation results into decimal numbers for display. This can result in a certain
   amount of error.

      (Example:)

      PR I NT 8 1 7. 3 - 8 1 0. 4  Correct result is 6.9.
        6. 8 9 9 9 9 9

ｷ Approximations are made during calculation of functions and exponentiation.
ｷ The above must be considered when using IF statements.

      (Example:)                              :GOTO 4 0

      10 A=1/100X100
      2 0 IF A = 1 THEN PR I N T " T R U E "
      30 PRINT "FALSE"
      4 0 PR I NT " A = " ;A
      5 0 END
      RUN
      FALSE
      A= 1

   Although the practical result of the equation in line 10 is 1, this program prints FALSE because of
error due to conversion.

202-
ｷ Notes concerning handling

ｷ Power switch
       The power switch should be left untouched for at least 10 seconds after being turned on or off.
       This is necessary to ensure correct operation of the computer. Do not unplug the power cable when
       the power switch is on: otherwise, trouble may result.

ｷ Power cable
       Avoid placing heavy objects such as desks on top of the power cable. This may damage the power
       cable, possibly resulting in a serious accident. Be sure to grasp the cable by the plug when unplugging
       it.

ｷ Power supply voltage
       The power supply voltage is 240/220 VAC. The computer may not operate properly if the voltage
       is too high or too low. Contact your dealer for assistance if you experience this problem.

ｷ Ventilation
       Many vents are provided in the cabinet to prevent overheating. Place the computer in a well ventilat-
       ed place, and do not cover it with a cloth. Do not place any objects on the left side of the computer,
       since this is where the vents for the power supply unit are located.

ｷ Humidity and dust
       Do not use the computer in a damp or dusty places.

ｷ Temperature
       Do not place the computer near heaters or in places where it may be exposed to direct sunlight;
       failure to observe this precaution may result in damage to the computer's components.

ｷ Water and foreign substances
       Water and other foreign substances (such as pins) entering the computer will damage it. Unplug
       the power cable immediately and contact your dealer for assistance if such an accident occurs.

ｷ Shock
       Avoid subjecting the computer to shock; strong shocks will damage the computer permanently.

ｷ Trouble
       Stop immediately operation and contact your dealer if you note any abnormality.

ｷ Prolonged disuse
       Be sure to unplug the power cable if the computer is not to be used for a prolonged period of time.

ｷ Connection of peripheral devices
       Use only parts and components designated by Sharp when connecting any peripheral devices, other-
       wise, the computer may be damaged.

ｷ Dirt
       Wipe the cabinet with a soft cloth soaked in water or detergent when it becomes dirty. To avoid
       discoloration of the cabinet, do not use volatile fluids such as benzene.

                                                                                                                                                      203-
     ｷ Noise
            It is recommended that a line filter be used when the computer is used in a place where high level
            noise signals may be present in the AC power. (A line filter can be obtained from your Sharp dealer).
            Move the signal cables as far as possible from the power cable and other electrical appliances.

     ｷ RF interference
            Interference with TV or radio reception may occur due to the RF signal generated by the computer
            if it is used near a TV or radio set. TV sets generate a strong magnetic field which may result in
            incorrect operation of the computer. If this occurs, move the TV set at least 2 to 3 meters away
            from the computer.

             This apparatus complies with requirements of EEC directive 76/889/EEC.

Copying/Debugging of MZ-700 Basic Interpreter

A. Please follow the procedure below mentioned to copy the BASIC tape.
    1) Power on MZ-700 (->ｷ m o n i t o r state)
    2) Partial memory should be modified by the use of monitor command M (memory correction) as
         follows:

         *MCF00
         CFOO F F - > CD
         CF01 00 27
         CF02 FF - > 00
         CF03 00 -y 38
         CF04 FF 03
         CF05 00 - > CD
         CF06 FF --> 2A
         CF07 00 - > 00
         CF08 F F -y DA
         CF09 00 - ｻ FE
         CFOA FF 00
         CFOB 00 - > C3
         CFOC F F --r AD
         CFOD 00 00
         CFOE FF CD
         CFOF 00 27
         CF10 FF 00
         CF11 00 - > 38
         CF12 FF F5
         CF13 00 C3
         CF14 F F CB
         CF15 00 - > OF

         I SHIFT | + BREAK | to be keyed in.
         NOTE: The content of memory from CFOO to CF15 may not always be as above mentioned.

    3) The cassette to be read (copyed from) should be set to the tape recorder.
    4) Key in the monitor command J (Jump) as follows:

         * JCFOO [CR]
         ｱ PLAY

         NOTE: If a button of the tape recorder is still pushed no play indication will appear.

    5) Confirming the " J . P L A Y " indication above mentioned, push I PLAY | button and load the content
         of BASIC tape. On this occasion, no indication like FILE NAME, etc. will be shown. When ERROR
         occured, please restart from the item 1) again.

    6) Set a new cassette to which the BASIC should be written into the recorder and execute | REWIND ] .
7) Key in as follows:

X J 1 1 0 8 [CR]

8) The monitor will be cleared and the following indication will appear:

   S-BASICEX SAVER xx GS xx 25
   HIT ANY KEY?

9) Push any key.

ｱ Record Play
I STOP | button should be pushed beforehand.

10) Push | RECORD"! button. The copy will start and the following indication will appear:

   WRITING S-BASIC

      On the occasion of MZ-711, item 9) should be effectuated after setting the external tape recorder
      in recording state.
11) After the sound "Pit Pit", the copy will be terminated.
12) The monitor state will be recovered by pushing the rear RESET SW.
13) Rewind the tape and push I STOP! button.
14) Key in as follows:

X JCFOE [CR|
ｱ PLAY

15) Push | PLAY | button of the recorder and the " V E R I F Y " function will be executed. When success-
      ful verified, the indication of "OK!" will appear though no other indication like FILE NAME etc.
      will appear. When error occured, please restart from the item 4).

16) Please make sure to enable the write protection of the cassette by removing the nail.

B. The following procedure is requested to modify the content of BASIC interpreter.
   a) Operate just as the case for copying mentioned in item 1) to 5).
   b) Call up the address to be modified by using the monitor command M.
        Ex. 8A in 1234H should be changed to 7A.

XM                     Key in
                       1234
1234  8A               7 A [CR|

1235  8A                  SHIFT 1 + I BREAK

X

C. The operation from the item 6) onwards should be continued hereafter.
